\n \n

\n\n

\n Paper  | \n Blog Post  | \n Demo  | \n Models  | \n Data\n

\n\n---\n\n**MolmoWeb** is an open multimodal web agent built by [Ai2](https://allenai.org). Given a natural-language task, MolmoWeb autonomously controls a web browser -- clicking, typing, scrolling, and navigating -- to complete the task. This repository contains the agent code, inference client, evaluation benchmarks, and everything needed to reproduce the results from the paper.\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n- [Models](#models)\n- [Installation](#installation)\n- [Quick Start](#quick-start)\n - [Download the Model](#1-download-the-model)\n - [Start the Model Server](#2-start-the-model-server)\n - [Test the Model](#3-test-the-model)\n- [Inference Client](#inference-client)\n - [Single Query](#single-query)\n - [Batch Queries](#batch-queries)\n - [Extract Accessibility Tree](#extract-accessibility-tree)\n- [Benchmarks](#benchmarks)\n- [Annotation Tool](annotation/README.md)\n- [Training](#training)\n - [Setup](#setup)\n - [Downloading Data](#downloading-data)\n - [Visualizing Data](#visualizing-data)\n - [Downloading Pretrained Checkpoints](#downloading-pretrained-checkpoints)\n - [SFT Training](#sft-training)\n- [Grounding Evaluation](#grounding-evaluation)\n- [Citation](#citation)\n- [License](#license)\n\n---\n\n## Models\n\n| Model | Parameters | HuggingFace |\n|-------|-----------|-------------|\n| MolmoWeb-8B | 8B | [allenai/MolmoWeb-8B](https://huggingface.co/allenai/MolmoWeb-8B) |\n| MolmoWeb-4B | 4B | [allenai/MolmoWeb-4B](https://huggingface.co/allenai/MolmoWeb-4B) |\n| MolmoWeb-8B-Native | 8B | [allenai/MolmoWeb-8B-Native](https://huggingface.co/allenai/MolmoWeb-8B-Native) |\n| MolmoWeb-4B-Native | 4B | [allenai/MolmoWeb-4B-Native](https://huggingface.co/allenai/MolmoWeb-4B-Native) |\n\nThe first two models (MolmoWeb-8B and MolmoWeb-4B) are Huggingface/transformers-compatible (see [example usage](https://huggingface.co/allenai/MolmoWeb-8B#quick-start) on Huggingface); and the last two (MolmoWeb-8B-Native and MolmoWeb-4B-Native) are molmo-native checkpoints. \n\n**Collections:**\n- [All MolmoWeb Models](https://huggingface.co/collections/allenai/molmoweb)\n- [MolmoWeb Training Data](https://huggingface.co/collections/allenai/molmoweb-data)\n\n---\n\n## Installation\n\nRequires Python >=3.10,<3.13. We use [uv](https://docs.astral.sh/uv/) for dependency management.\n\n```bash\n# Install uv if you don't have it\ncurl -LsSf https://astral.sh/uv/install.sh | sh\n\n# Clone and install\ngit clone git@github.com:allenai/molmoweb.git\ncd molmoweb\nuv venv --python \">=3.10,<3.13\"\nuv sync\n\n# Install Playwright browsers (needed for local browser control)\nuv run playwright install\nuv run playwright install --with-deps chromium\n```\n\n---\n\n### Environment Variables\n\n```bash\n# Browserbase (required when --env_type browserbase)\nexport BROWSERBASE_API_KEY=\"your-browserbase-api-key\"\nexport BROWSERBASE_PROJECT_ID=\"your-browserbase-project-id\"\n\n# Google Gemini (required for gemini_cua, gemini_axtree, and Gemini-based judges)\nexport GOOGLE_API_KEY=\"your-google-api-key\"\n\n# OpenAI (required for gpt_axtree and GPT-based judges like webvoyager)\nexport OPENAI_API_KEY=\"your-openai-api-key\"\n```\n\n---\n\n## Quick Start\n\nThree helper scripts in `scripts/` let you download weights, start the server, and test it end-to-end.\n\n### 1. Download the Model\n\n```bash\nbash scripts/download_weights.sh # MolmoWeb-8B (default)\nbash scripts/download_weights.sh allenai/MolmoWeb-4B-Native # MolmoWeb-4B Native\n```\n\nThis downloads the weights to `./checkpoints/`.\n\n### 2. Start the Model Server\n\n```bash\n# default predictor type is native\nbash scripts/start_server.sh ./checkpoints/MolmoWeb-4B-Native # MolmoWeb-4B-Native\n# change to HF-compatible\nexport PREDICTOR_TYPE=\"hf\"\nbash scripts/start_server.sh ./checkpoints/MolmoWeb-8B # MolmoWeb-8B, port 8001\nbash scripts/start_server.sh ./checkpoints/MolmoWeb-8B 8002 # custom port\n```\n\nOr configure via environment variables:\n\n```bash\nexport CKPT=\"./checkpoints/MolmoWeb-4B-Native\" # local path to downloaded weights\nexport PREDICTOR_TYPE=\"native\" # \"native\" or \"hf\"\nexport NUM_PREDICTORS=1 # number of GPU workers\n\nbash scripts/start_server.sh\n```\n\nThe server exposes a single endpoint:\n\n```\nPOST http://127.0.0.1:8001/predict\n{\n \"prompt\": \"...\",\n \"image_base64\": \"...\"\n}\n```\n\nWait for the server to print that the model is loaded, then test it.\n\n### 3. Test the Model\n\nOnce the server is running, send it a screenshot of the [Ai2 careers page](https://allenai.org/careers) (included in `assets/test_screenshot.png`) and ask it to read the job titles:\n\n```bash\nuv run python scripts/test_server.py # default: localhost:8001\nuv run python scripts/test_server.py http://myhost:8002 # custom endpoint\n```\n\nThe test script sends this prompt to the model:\n\n> Read the text on this page. What are the first four job titles listed under 'Open roles'?\n\nYou can also do it manually in a few lines of Python:\n\n```python\nimport base64, requests\n\nwith open(\"assets/test_screenshot.png\", \"rb\") as f:\n image_b64 = base64.b64encode(f.read()).decode()\n\nresp = requests.post(\"http://127.0.0.1:8001/predict\", json={\n \"prompt\": \"What are the first four job titles listed under 'Open roles'?\",\n \"image_base64\": image_b64,\n})\nprint(resp.json())\n```\n\n---\n\n## Inference Client\n\nThe `inference` package provides a high-level Python client that manages a browser session and runs the agent end-to-end. The client communicates with a running model server endpoint.\n\n### Single Query\n\n```python\nfrom inference import MolmoWeb\n\nclient = MolmoWeb(\n endpoint=\"SET_UP_YOUR_ENDPOINT\",\n local=True, # True = local Chromium, False = Browserbase cloud browser\n headless=True,\n) \n\nquery = \"Go to arxiv.org and find out the paper about Molmo and Pixmo.\"\ntraj = client.run(query=query, max_steps=10)\n\noutput_path = traj.save_html(query=query)\nprint(f\"Saved to {output_path}\")\n```\n\n### Follow-up Query\n\n```python\nfollowup_query = \"Find the full author list of the paper.\"\ntraj2 = client.continue_run(query=followup_query, max_steps=10)\n```\n\n### Batch Queries\n\n```python\nqueries = [\n \"Go to allenai.org and find the latest research papers on top of the homepage\",\n \"Search for 'OLMo' on Wikipedia\",\n \"What is the weather in Seattle today?\",\n]\n\ntrajectories = client.run_batch(\n queries=queries,\n max_steps=10,\n max_workers=3,\n) # Inspect the trajectory .html files default saved under inference/htmls\n```\n\n### Inference Backends\n\nSupported backends: `fastapi` (remote HTTP endpoint), `modal` (serverless), `native` (native molmo/olmo-compatible checkpoint), `hf` (HuggingFace Transformers-compatible checkpoint).\n\n> **vLLM support**: We leave vLLM integration to users. Please be cautious, as vLLM does not support the exact attention backend used in OLMo, which may lead to unexpected behavior or reduced accuracy.\n\n### Extract Accessibility Tree\n\n```\nfrom inference.client import MolmoWeb\n\nclient = MolmoWeb()\naxtree_str = client.get_axtree(\"https://allenai.org/\")\nprint(axtree_str)\nclient.close()\n```\n\n---\n\n## Benchmarks\n\nThe `benchmarks/` directory contains the unified evaluation framework. It supports five benchmarks out of the box: **WebVoyager**, **Online Mind2Web**, **DeepShop**, **WebTailBench**, and **Custom** (bring your own tasks).\n\nThe evaluation pipeline has two stages:\n\n1. **Run** -- the agent executes tasks in a browser, producing trajectory logs.\n2. **Judge** -- an LLM judge scores each trajectory for success.\n\n### Running Evaluations\n\nThe entry point is `benchmarks/benchmarks.py`, a [Fire](https://github.com/google/python-fire) CLI with two commands: `run` and `judge`.\n\n```bash\nuv run python -m benchmarks.benchmarks run \\\n --benchmark custom \\\n --data_path ./demo_task.json \\\n --results_dir ./results \\\n --agent_type molmoweb \\\n --inference_mode fastapi \\\n --endpoint_or_checkpoint http://127.0.0.1:8001 \\\n --max_steps 30 \\\n --num_workers 1 \\\n --env_type simple\n```\n\n### Judging Results\n\nAfter trajectories are collected, run the judge. The `webvoyager` judge requires `OPENAI_API_KEY` to be set.\n\n```bash\nuv run python -m benchmarks.benchmarks judge \\\n --benchmark custom \\\n --data_path ./demo_task.json \\\n --results_dir ./results \\\n --judge_type webvoyager \\\n --num_workers 1\n```\n\n### Synthetic Data Generation\n\nThe same evaluation framework can be used to generate synthetic training data by running other agents on tasks. Collect trajectories with any supported agent and use the resulting logs for training.\n\n### Agents\n\n| Agent | Description | Required Environment Variables |\n|-------|-------------|-------------------------------|\n| `molmoweb` | MolmoWeb multimodal agent (local model server) | None (uses `--endpoint_or_checkpoint`) |\n| `gemini_cua` | Gemini computer-use agent | `GOOGLE_API_KEY` |\n| `gemini_axtree` | Gemini with accessibility tree | `GOOGLE_API_KEY` |\n| `gpt_axtree` | GPT with accessibility tree | `OPENAI_API_KEY` |\n\nWe welcome contributions of custom agents. To add your own, implement the agent interface in `agent/` and register the agent type in `benchmarks/evaluate.py`.\n\n### Evaluating Other Agents on Benchmarks\n\nYou can evaluate any supported agent on any benchmark using the same code. For example, to evaluate `gemini_axtree` on Online Mind2Web with Browserbase:\n\n```bash\nuv run python -m benchmarks.benchmarks run \\\n --benchmark online_mind2web \\\n --results_dir ./results/om2w_gemini_axtree \\\n --agent_type gemini_axtree \\\n --max_steps 30 \\\n --num_workers 5 \\\n --env_type browserbase\n```\n\nThen judge the results:\n\n```bash\nuv run python -m benchmarks.benchmarks judge \\\n --benchmark online_mind2web \\\n --results_dir ./results/om2w_gemini_axtree \\\n --judge_type webjudge_online_mind2web \\\n --num_workers 5\n```\n\n### benchmarks.py Reference\n\n#### `run` command\n\n| Argument | Type | Default | Description |\n|----------|------|---------|-------------|\n| `results_dir` | `str` | *(required)* | Output directory for trajectory logs. |\n| `agent_type` | `str` | *(required)* | Agent to use: `molmoweb`, `gemini_cua`, `gemini_axtree`, or `gpt_axtree`. |\n| `benchmark` | `str` | `\"custom\"` | Benchmark name: `custom`, `deepshop`, `webvoyager`, `online_mind2web`, or `webtailbench`. |\n| `data_path` | `str` | `None` | Override the default data file path for the chosen benchmark. |\n| `inference_mode` | `str` | `None` | How to connect to the model: `fastapi` (HTTP endpoint), `local` (in-process HF), `modal` (Modal serverless), or `native` (in-process OLMo). |\n| `endpoint_or_checkpoint` | `str` | `None` | Either an HTTP URL (for `fastapi`/`modal`) or a local path / HF model ID (for `local`/`native`). |\n| `device` | `str` | `None` | CUDA device for local inference, e.g. `cuda:0`. |\n| `api_key` | `str` | `None` | API key for API-based agents (Gemini, GPT). |\n| `num_workers` | `int` | `5` | Number of parallel evaluation workers. |\n| `max_steps` | `int` | `30` | Maximum agent steps per episode. |\n| `env_type` | `str` | `\"simple\"` | Browser environment: `browserbase` (requires `BROWSERBASE_API_KEY` and `BROWSERBASE_PROJECT_ID`) or `simple` (local Chromium). |\n\n#### `judge` command\n\n| Argument | Type | Default | Description |\n|----------|------|---------|-------------|\n| `results_dir` | `str` | *(required)* | Directory containing trajectory logs to judge. |\n| `benchmark` | `str` | `\"custom\"` | Benchmark name (must match what was used during `run`). |\n| `data_path` | `str` | `None` | Override data file path. |\n| `judge_type` | `str` | `None` | Judge implementation. Defaults to the benchmark's default judge. Options: `webvoyager` (GPT-4o), `deepshop_judge`, `webjudge_online_mind2web`. |\n| `num_workers` | `int` | `30` | Number of parallel judging workers. |\n\nSee [benchmarks/README.md](benchmarks/README.md) for full documentation.\n\n---\n\n## Training\n\nTraining code lives in the `train/` directory. MolmoWeb training is a single-stage SFT on top of a Molmo2 pretrained checkpoint.\n\n### Setup\n\nInstall dependencies inside the `train/` directory:\n\n```bash\ncd train\nuv sync\n```\n\nSet the following environment variables (used by training, eval, and data scripts):\n\n```bash\nexport WEBOLMO_DATA_DIR=/path/to/datasets # MolmoWeb training data\n```\n\n### Downloading Data\n\nMolmoWeb training data is hosted on HuggingFace under the [MolmoWeb Data collection](https://huggingface.co/collections/allenai/molmoweb-data). With `WEBOLMO_DATA_DIR` set, download all datasets with:\n\n```bash\nuv run python olmo/data/download_datasets.py\n```\n\n| Dataset | HuggingFace Repo | Description |\n|---|---|---|\n| SyntheticGround | `allenai/MolmoWeb-SyntheticGround` | Synthetic web grounding (click targets) |\n| SyntheticQA | `allenai/MolmoWeb-SyntheticQA` | Synthetic screenshot QA |\n| SyntheticTrajs | `allenai/MolmoWeb-SyntheticTrajs` | Gemini-generated agent trajectories |\n| HumanTrajs | `allenai/MolmoWeb-HumanTrajs` | Human-annotated trajectories |\n| SyntheticSkills | `allenai/MolmoWeb-SyntheticSkills` | Synthetic atomic skill demonstrations |\n| HumanSkills | `allenai/MolmoWeb-HumanSkills` | Human atomic skill demonstrations |\n| PixMoPoints | `allenai/pixmo-points` | Point annotations for visual grounding |\n| ScreenSpot | `rootsautomation/ScreenSpot` | UI grounding benchmark |\n| ScreenSpotV2 | `likaixin/ScreenSpot-v2-variants` | UI grounding benchmark v2 |\n\n### Visualizing Data\n\nTo inspect dataset examples as an HTML file, run `dataset_visualize.py` from inside the `train/` directory:\n\n```bash\nuv run python dataset_visualize.py \n```\n\nFor example, to visualize 50 shuffled training examples from `molmoweb_synthetic_trajs`:\n\n```bash\nuv run python dataset_visualize.py molmoweb_synthetic_trajs ./viz --split train --num_examples 50 --shuffle\n```\n\nThis saves `./viz/molmoweb_synthetic_trajs.html` with rendered examples (images, tokenized text, and ground-truth annotations).\n\n### Downloading Pretrained Checkpoints\n\nSFT training starts from a Molmo2 pretrained checkpoint. Download one of the pretrained base checkpoints from HuggingFace:\n\n```bash\nbash scripts/download_weights.sh allenai/MolmoWeb-Pretrained-8B # 8B base\nbash scripts/download_weights.sh allenai/MolmoWeb-Pretrained-4B # 4B base\n```\n\nThis saves the checkpoint to `./checkpoints/MolmoWeb-Pretrained-8B` (or `-4B`). Set `CHECKPOINT_PATH` in `train/run_train.sh` to this path before launching training.\n\n| Model | HuggingFace Repo |\n|---|---|\n| MolmoWeb-Pretrained-8B | [allenai/MolmoWeb-Pretrained-8B](https://huggingface.co/allenai/MolmoWeb-Pretrained-8B) |\n| MolmoWeb-Pretrained-4B | [allenai/MolmoWeb-Pretrained-4B](https://huggingface.co/allenai/MolmoWeb-Pretrained-4B) |\n\n### SFT Training\n\nConfigure the variables at the top of `train/run_train.sh`, then run:\n\n```bash\ncd train\nbash run_train.sh\n```\n\n| Variable | Default | Description |\n|---|---|---|\n| `CHECKPOINT_PATH` | MolmoWeb-Pretrained-4B | Path to pretrained starting checkpoint |\n| `MIXTURE` | `molmoweb` | Data mixture (`molmoweb` or `debug`) |\n| `NUM_GPUS` | `8` | GPUs per node |\n| `GLOBAL_BATCH_SIZE` | `64` | Total batch size across all GPUs |\n| `DEVICE_BATCH_SIZE` | `2` | Per-GPU batch size |\n| `SEQ_LEN` | `10240` | Sequence length |\n| `DURATION` | `500` | Number of training steps |\n| `SAVE_INTERVAL` | `100` | Checkpoint save frequency (steps) |\n\nTo launch a debug run directly:\n\n```bash\nuv run torchrun -m --nproc-per-node 1 \\\n launch_scripts.train debug debug \\\n --save_folder=dbg \\\n --device_batch_size 1 \\\n --duration 10 \\\n --global_batch_size 2\n```\n---\n\n## Grounding Evaluation\n\nMolmoWeb can be evaluated on grounding benchmarks to measure how accurately the model predicts click coordinates for UI elements.\n\n| Benchmark | Task name The repository provides the complete agent implementation, pretrained model weights (4B and 8B parameter variants), inference clients, evaluation benchmarks, and training code necessary to reproduce the research results or build upon the system. Tome

\n\n

\n Local meeting capture → Obsidian vault → AI agent pipeline. No cloud. No API keys. Your data.\n

\n\n

\n \n \n \n \n

\n\n---\n\nTome is a macOS app that captures meetings and voice memos, transcribes them locally with Parakeet-TDT v3, and drops structured `.md` files straight into your Obsidian vault. Everything runs on-device. Nothing phones home.\n\n

\n \n \n

\n\n## Background\n\nI'm a consultant who fell down the Obsidian rabbit hole. I built out a vault as a second brain: structured notes with YAML frontmatter, backlinks, tags, and a Claude agent layer that processes everything. Client files, meeting notes, action items, daily briefs, all flowing through the vault automatically.\n\nThe problem was capture. I'm on calls all day and I don't take notes. I needed something that would listen, transcribe, and drop structured markdown into the vault where my agent could pick it up and do the rest. Pull out action items, update client files, connect the dots.\n\nI looked at Otter, Granola, Fireflies. They all lock your data in their cloud, their format, their walled garden. None of them output plain markdown. None of them are built to feed into an agent workflow.\n\nI started from [OpenGranola](https://github.com/yazinsai/OpenGranola), learned Swift along the way, and rebuilt it with a different audio pipeline, local ASR, speaker diarization, and vault-native output. If you're running Obsidian with any kind of AI agent setup, you probably have the same gap.\n\n## Why Tome?\n\n- **Plain markdown out.** YAML frontmatter, tags, timestamps. Your vault already knows what to do with it. No proprietary export, no copy-paste, no middleman.\n- **Built for the agent pipeline.** Tome is just the capture layer. You talk, it transcribes, your agent picks up the `.md` and does whatever you've wired it to do.\n- **Runs on your machine.** Parakeet-TDT v3 on Apple Silicon. No API keys, no accounts, no subscriptions, no data leaving the building.\n\n```\nspeak → capture → vault → agent → knowledge base\n```\n\nTome does the first three. Your agent does the rest.\n\n## Features\n\n- **Multilingual transcription** via Parakeet-TDT v3 ([FluidAudio](https://github.com/FluidInference/FluidAudio)) on Apple Silicon. 25 European languages, auto-detected. Nothing hits the network.\n- **Call Capture** grabs mic + system audio. Detects which conferencing app you're in (Teams, Zoom, Slack, etc.) and filters audio to just that app. Your Spotify and notification sounds stay out of the transcript.\n- **Voice Memo** is mic only. For quick thoughts, verbal notes, stream of consciousness. Saves to a separate folder so it doesn't clutter your meeting transcripts.\n- **Speaker diarization** runs after the call ends. pyannote splits the remote audio into Speaker 2, Speaker 3, Speaker 4. Not perfect, but way better than one wall of unattributed text.\n- **Vault-native output** writes `.md` with frontmatter: `type`, `created`, `attendees`, `tags`, `source_app`. Lands in your vault ready to process.\n- **Privacy.** Hidden from screen sharing by default. No audio saved. Transcripts only.\n- **Silence auto-stop.** 120 seconds of dead air and it stops itself.\n\n## How It Works\n\n```\n┌─────────────┐ ┌──────────────────┐ ┌───────────────┐\n│ Microphone │────▶│ │ │ │\n└─────────────┘ │ Tome │ │ Obsidian │\n │ ┌────────────┐ │────▶│ Vault │\n┌─────────────┐ │ │ Parakeet │ │ │ (.md files) │\n│ System │────▶│ │ TDT v3 │ │ │ │\n│ Audio │ │ └────────────┘ │ └───────┬───────┘\n└─────────────┘ └──────────────────┘ │\n ▼\n ┌──────────────┐\n │ AI Agent │\n │ Layer │\n │ (notes, │\n │ actions, │\n │ updates) │\n └──────────────┘\n```\n\n1. **Capture** picks up mic audio + system audio from a specific conferencing app via ScreenCaptureKit.\n2. **Transcribe** runs VAD to detect speech segments, then Parakeet transcribes locally.\n3. **Diarize** splits the system audio into individual speakers after the session ends.\n4. **Write** drops structured `.md` with YAML frontmatter into your vault folder.\n5. **Agent picks up** whatever you've got downstream processes the transcript.\n\n## Output\n\n

\n \n

\n\n

\n \n

\n\n```markdown\n---\ntype: meeting\ncreated: \"2026-03-23\"\ntime: \"10:00\"\nduration: \"18:42\"\nsource_app: \"Zoom\"\nattendees: [\"You\", \"Speaker 2\"]\ntags:\n - log/meeting\n - status/inbox\n - source/tome\n---\n\n# Call Recording — 2026-03-23 10:00\n\n**You** (10:00:03)\nMorning. Quick sync on the product launch. Where are we at?\n\n**Speaker 2** (10:00:07)\nWe're in good shape. QA signed off yesterday, marketing assets\nare locked, landing page is live in staging.\n```\n\nVoice memos use `type: fleeting` with a single speaker. Same structure, same frontmatter.\n\n## Build\n\n**Requirements:** Apple Silicon Mac, macOS 26+, Xcode 26.3+\n\n```bash\ngit clone https://github.com/Gremble-io/Tome.git\ncd Tome\n./scripts/build_swift_app.sh\n```\n\nBuilds and installs to `/Applications`. First launch downloads the Parakeet ASR model (~600MB, cached after that).\n\n**Dev build:**\n\n```bash\ncd Tome\nswift build\n```\n\n## Permissions\n\n| Permission | When | Why |\n|---|---|---|\n| **Microphone** | All modes | Captures your voice |\n| **Screen Recording** | Call Capture only | ScreenCaptureKit needs this for system audio from conferencing apps |\n\nmacOS re-prompts for Screen Recording permission roughly monthly. That's an OS thing, not Tome.\n\n## Architecture\n\n```\nTome/Sources/Tome/\n├── App/\n│ ├── TomeApp.swift # App entry point\n│ └── AppUpdaterController.swift # Sparkle update controller\n├── Audio/\n│ ├── SystemAudioCapture.swift # ScreenCaptureKit + per-app filtering\n│ └── MicCapture.swift # AVAudioEngine mic input\n├── Models/\n│ ├── Models.swift # Domain types (Utterance, Speaker, etc.)\n│ └── TranscriptStore.swift # Observable transcript state\n├── Transcription/\n│ ├── TranscriptionEngine.swift # Dual-stream capture + diarization\n│ └── StreamingTranscriber.swift # VAD + Parakeet ASR pipeline\n├── Storage/\n│ ├── TranscriptLogger.swift # .md output with YAML frontmatter\n│ └── SessionStore.swift # Session metadata\n├── Settings/\n│ └── AppSettings.swift\n└── Views/\n ├── ContentView.swift\n ├── ControlBar.swift\n ├── TranscriptView.swift\n ├── WaveformView.swift\n ├── SettingsView.swift\n ├── OnboardingView.swift\n └── CheckForUpdatesView.swift\n```\n\n## Privacy\n\n- Transcription runs entirely on-device. No audio is ever sent anywhere.\n- No network calls. No analytics. No telemetry.\n- No audio is saved to disk. Only text transcripts.\n- The app window is hidden from screen sharing by default.\n- Transcripts are saved as plain `.md` files to a folder you choose.\n\n## Known Limitations\n\n- **Apple Silicon only.** Parakeet and FluidAudio need Metal / ANE. No Intel.\n- **macOS 26+ only.**\n- **Screen Recording re-prompts monthly.** OS limitation.\n- **Diarization is imperfect.** Works well with headset mics. Laptop speakers with crosstalk will give you worse speaker separation.\n- **No live speaker labels.** Diarization runs after the session ends. During the call, remote audio shows as a single stream.\n\n## Troubleshooting\n\n**\"Tome is damaged and can't be opened\"**\n\nThis is macOS Gatekeeper blocking an unsigned app. Until a signed release is available:\n\n1. Right-click (or Control-click) `Tome.app` in `/Applications`\n2. Click **Open**\n3. In the dialog, click **Open** again\n\nYou only need to do this once — after that, Tome launches normally.\n\nAlternatively, build from source (see [Build](#build) above) to avoid Gatekeeper entirely.\n\n## Credits\n\nStarted from [OpenGranola](https://github.com/yazinsai/OpenGranola). Substantially rewritten from there.\n\n## License\n\n[MIT](LICENSE)\n","summary":" Tome is a privacy-focused macOS application that captures meetings and voice memos, transcribes them locally using Parakeet-TDT v3, and deposits structured Markdown files directly into an Obsidian vault for AI agent processing. Unlike cloud-based transcription services, it operates entirely on-device with no API keys or network connectivity, featuring speaker diarization, multilingual support for 25 European languages, and intelligent audio filtering that isolates conferencing applications like Zoom or Teams. The app outputs vault-native markdown with YAML frontmatter, timestamps, and attendee tags, creating a seamless pipeline from speech to structured knowledge without data ever leaving the user's machine. Free) or OpenAI API key.**\n - Usage will contribute to your Codex usage limits. [Learn more](https://developers.openai.com/codex/pricing).\n- **Node.js 18.18 or later**\n\n## Install\n\nAdd the marketplace in Claude Code:\n\n```bash\n/plugin marketplace add openai/codex-plugin-cc\n```\n\nInstall the plugin:\n\n```bash\n/plugin install codex@openai-codex\n```\n\nReload plugins:\n\n```bash\n/reload-plugins\n```\n\nThen run:\n\n```bash\n/codex:setup\n```\n\n`/codex:setup` will tell you whether Codex is ready. If Codex is missing and npm is available, it can offer to install Codex for you.\n\nIf you prefer to install Codex yourself, use:\n\n```bash\nnpm install -g @openai/codex\n```\n\nIf Codex is installed but not logged in yet, run:\n\n```bash\n!codex login\n```\n\nAfter install, you should see:\n\n- the slash commands listed below\n- the `codex:codex-rescue` subagent in `/agents`\n\nOne simple first run is:\n\n```bash\n/codex:review --background\n/codex:status\n/codex:result\n```\n\n## Usage\n\n### `/codex:review`\n\nRuns a normal Codex review on your current work. It gives you the same quality of code review as running `/review` inside Codex directly.\n\n> [!NOTE]\n> Code review especially for multi-file changes might take a while. It's generally recommended to run it in the background.\n\nUse it when you want:\n\n- a review of your current uncommitted changes\n- a review of your branch compared to a base branch like `main`\n\nUse `--base ` for branch review. It also supports `--wait` and `--background`. It is not steerable and does not take custom focus text. Use [`/codex:adversarial-review`](#codexadversarial-review) when you want to challenge a specific decision or risk area.\n\nExamples:\n\n```bash\n/codex:review\n/codex:review --base main\n/codex:review --background\n```\n\nThis command is read-only and will not perform any changes. When run in the background you can use [`/codex:status`](#codexstatus) to check on the progress and [`/codex:cancel`](#codexcancel) to cancel the ongoing task.\n\n### `/codex:adversarial-review`\n\nRuns a **steerable** review that questions the chosen implementation and design.\n\nIt can be used to pressure-test assumptions, tradeoffs, failure modes, and whether a different approach would have been safer or simpler.\n\nIt uses the same review target selection as `/codex:review`, including `--base ` for branch review.\nIt also supports `--wait` and `--background`. Unlike `/codex:review`, it can take extra focus text after the flags.\n\nUse it when you want:\n\n- a review before shipping that challenges the direction, not just the code details\n- review focused on design choices, tradeoffs, hidden assumptions, and alternative approaches\n- pressure-testing around specific risk areas like auth, data loss, rollback, race conditions, or reliability\n\nExamples:\n\n```bash\n/codex:adversarial-review\n/codex:adversarial-review --base main challenge whether this was the right caching and retry design\n/codex:adversarial-review --background look for race conditions and question the chosen approach\n```\n\nThis command is read-only. It does not fix code.\n\n### `/codex:rescue`\n\nHands a task to Codex through the `codex:codex-rescue` subagent.\n\nUse it when you want Codex to:\n\n- investigate a bug\n- try a fix\n- continue a previous Codex task\n- take a faster or cheaper pass with a smaller model\n\n> [!NOTE]\n> Depending on the task and the model you choose these tasks might take a long time and it's generally recommended to force the task to be in the background or move the agent to the background.\n\nIt supports `--background`, `--wait`, `--resume`, and `--fresh`. If you omit `--resume` and `--fresh`, the plugin can offer to continue the latest rescue thread for this repo.\n\nExamples:\n\n```bash\n/codex:rescue investigate why the tests started failing\n/codex:rescue fix the failing test with the smallest safe patch\n/codex:rescue --resume apply the top fix from the last run\n/codex:rescue --model gpt-5.4-mini --effort medium investigate the flaky integration test\n/codex:rescue --model spark fix the issue quickly\n/codex:rescue --background investigate the regression\n```\n\nYou can also just ask for a task to be delegated to Codex:\n\n```text\nAsk Codex to redesign the database connection to be more resilient.\n```\n\n**Notes:**\n\n- if you do not pass `--model` or `--effort`, Codex chooses its own defaults.\n- if you say `spark`, the plugin maps that to `gpt-5.3-codex-spark`\n- follow-up rescue requests can continue the latest Codex task in the repo\n\n### `/codex:status`\n\nShows running and recent Codex jobs for the current repository.\n\nExamples:\n\n```bash\n/codex:status\n/codex:status task-abc123\n```\n\nUse it to:\n\n- check progress on background work\n- see the latest completed job\n- confirm whether a task is still running\n\n### `/codex:result`\n\nShows the final stored Codex output for a finished job.\nWhen available, it also includes the Codex session ID so you can reopen that run directly in Codex with `codex resume `.\n\nExamples:\n\n```bash\n/codex:result\n/codex:result task-abc123\n```\n\n### `/codex:cancel`\n\nCancels an active background Codex job.\n\nExamples:\n\n```bash\n/codex:cancel\n/codex:cancel task-abc123\n```\n\n### `/codex:setup`\n\nChecks whether Codex is installed and authenticated.\nIf Codex is missing and npm is available, it can offer to install Codex for you.\n\nYou can also use `/codex:setup` to manage the optional review gate.\n\n#### Enabling review gate\n\n```bash\n/codex:setup --enable-review-gate\n/codex:setup --disable-review-gate\n```\n\nWhen the review gate is enabled, the plugin uses a `Stop` hook to run a targeted Codex review based on Claude's response. If that review finds issues, the stop is blocked so Claude can address them first.\n\n> [!WARNING]\n> The review gate can create a long-running Claude/Codex loop and may drain usage limits quickly. Only enable it when you plan to actively monitor the session.\n\n## Typical Flows\n\n### Review Before Shipping\n\n```bash\n/codex:review\n```\n\n### Hand A Problem To Codex\n\n```bash\n/codex:rescue investigate why the build is failing in CI\n```\n\n### Start Something Long-Running\n\n```bash\n/codex:adversarial-review --background\n/codex:rescue --background investigate the flaky test\n```\n\nThen check in with:\n\n```bash\n/codex:status\n/codex:result\n```\n\n## Codex Integration\n\nThe Codex plugin wraps the [Codex app server](https://developers.openai.com/codex/app-server). It uses the global `codex` binary installed in your environment and [applies the same configuration](https://developers.openai.com/codex/config-basic).\n\n### Common Configurations\n\nIf you want to change the default reasoning effort or the default model that gets used by the plugin, you can define that inside your user-level or project-level `config.toml`. For example to always use `gpt-5.4-mini` on `high` for a specific project you can add the following to a `.codex/config.toml` file at the root of the directory you started Claude in:\n\n```toml\nmodel = \"gpt-5.4-mini\"\nmodel_reasoning_effort = \"high\"\n```\n\nYour configuration will be picked up based on:\n\n- user-level config in `~/.codex/config.toml`\n- project-level overrides in `.codex/config.toml`\n- project-level overrides only load when the [project is trusted](https://developers.openai.com/codex/config-advanced#project-config-files-codexconfigtoml)\n\nCheck out the Codex docs for more [configuration options](https://developers.openai.com/codex/config-reference).\n\n### Moving The Work Over To Codex\n\nDelegated tasks and any [stop gate](#what-does-the-review-gate-do) run can also be directly resumed inside Codex by running `codex resume` either with the specific session ID you received from running `/codex:result` or `/codex:status` or by selecting it from the list.\n\nThis way you can review the Codex work or continue the work there.\n\n## FAQ\n\n### Do I need a separate Codex account for this plugin?\n\nIf you are already signed into Codex on this machine, that account should work immediately here too. This plugin uses your local Codex CLI authentication.\n\nIf you only use Claude Code today and have not used Codex yet, you will also need to sign in to Codex with either a ChatGPT account or an API key. [Codex is available with your ChatGPT subscription](https://developers.openai.com/codex/pricing/), and [`codex login`](https://developers.openai.com/codex/cli/reference/#codex-login) supports both ChatGPT and API key sign-in. Run `/codex:setup` to check whether Codex is ready, and use `!codex login` if it is not.\n\n### Does the plugin use a separate Codex runtime?\n\nNo. This plugin delegates through your local [Codex CLI](https://developers.openai.com/codex/cli/) and [Codex app server](https://developers.openai.com/codex/app-server/) on the same machine.\n\nThat means:\n\n- it uses the same Codex install you would use directly\n- it uses the same local authentication state\n- it uses the same repository checkout and machine-local environment\n\n### Will it use the same Codex config I already have?\n\nYes. \n \n

\n\n

Phantom

\n

An AI co-worker with its own computer.

\n\n

\n \n \n \n \n

\n\n

\n Website ·\n Get a Free Phantom ·\n Docs ·\n Issues\n

\n\n---\n\n## The Idea\n\nAI agents today are disposable. You open a chat, get an answer, close the tab, and the context is gone. Next time you start from scratch. Every session is day one.\n\nPhantom takes a different approach: **give the AI its own computer.** A dedicated machine where it installs software, spins up databases, builds dashboards, remembers what you told it last week, and gets measurably better at your job every day. Your laptop stays yours. The agent's workspace is its own.\n\nThis is not a chatbot. It is a co-worker that runs on Slack, has a web chat interface at `/chat`, has its own email address, creates its own tools, and builds infrastructure without asking for permission. Don't take our word for it - scroll down to see what production Phantoms have actually built.\n\n## What This Actually Looks Like\n\nThese are not mockups. They happened on production Phantom instances.\n\n### Built an analytics platform from scratch\n\nA Phantom was asked to help with data analysis. It installed ClickHouse on its own VM, downloaded the full Hacker News dataset, loaded 28.7 million rows spanning 2007-2021, built an analytics dashboard with interactive charts, and created a REST API to query the data. Then it registered that API as an MCP tool so it could use it in future sessions and other agents could query it too.\n\nNobody asked it to build any of this. It identified analytics as useful and built the entire stack.\n\n

\n \n

\n\n*28.7 million items. 755K unique authors. 4.3 million stories. Built, loaded, and served by a Phantom on its own machine.*\n\n### Extended itself with a channel it was never built with\n\nPhantom ships with Slack, Telegram, Email, and Webhook channels. It does not ship with Discord. When asked \"Can I talk to you on Discord?\", the Phantom said: \"Not right now. Discord isn't wired up. That said, I could build it.\"\n\nIt explained the Discord Bot API, walked the user through creating a Discord application, provided a magic link for secure token submission, and said: \"Once you save it, I'll automatically spin up the container and you'll be live on Discord.\"\n\nAfter submitting the token, Phantom went live on Discord. It permanently gained a communication channel it was never designed with.\n\n

\n \n

\n\n*The agent was honest about what it could not do, then built the capability on the spot.*\n\n### Started monitoring its own infrastructure\n\nA Phantom discovered [Vigil](https://github.com/baudsmithstudios/vigil), a lightweight open-source system monitor with 3 GitHub stars. It understood what Vigil does, integrated it into its existing ClickHouse instance, built a sync pipeline that batch-transfers metrics every 30 seconds, and created a real-time monitoring dashboard showing service health, Docker container status, network I/O, disk I/O, system load, and data pipeline health.\n\n890,450 rows. 25 metrics. Auto-refreshing. The agent is watching its own infrastructure.\n\n

\n \n

\n\n*It found a 3-star open-source project, integrated it into its data pipeline, and built observability for itself.*\n\n---\n\nThis is what happens when you give an AI its own computer.\n\n## Bring Your Own Model\n\nPhantom is not locked to any single AI backend. It ships with support for seven providers out of the box, configured through a single YAML block:\n\n- **Anthropic** (default) - Claude Opus, Sonnet, Haiku\n- **Z.AI** - GLM-5.1 and GLM-4.5-Air via [Z.AI's Anthropic-compatible API](https://docs.z.ai/guides/llm/glm-5). Roughly 15x cheaper than Claude Opus for comparable coding quality.\n- **OpenRouter** - 100+ models through one key\n- **Ollama** - Any GGUF model on your own GPU, zero API cost\n- **vLLM** - Self-hosted inference with OpenAI-compatible endpoints\n- **LiteLLM** - Local proxy bridging OpenAI, Gemini, and more\n- **Custom** - Any Anthropic Messages API compatible endpoint\n\nSwitching providers is two lines of YAML:\n\n```yaml\n# phantom.yaml\nmodel: claude-opus-4-7\nprovider:\n type: zai\n api_key_env: ZAI_API_KEY\n model_mappings:\n sonnet: glm-5.1\n```\n\nSet `ZAI_API_KEY` in `.env`, restart, done. Both the main agent and every evolution judge flow through the chosen provider from that point on. The tools are the same, the memory is the same, the self-evolution pipeline is the same. Only the brain changes.\n\nAnthropic stays the default. Existing deployments continue to work with no configuration changes. See [docs/providers.md](docs/providers.md) for the full reference.\n\n## Quick Start\n\n### Docker (recommended)\n\n```bash\ncurl -fsSL https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ghostwright/phantom/main/docker-compose.user.yaml -o docker-compose.yaml\ncurl -fsSL https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ghostwright/phantom/main/.env.example -o .env\n# Edit .env - add your ANTHROPIC_API_KEY, Slack tokens, and OWNER_SLACK_USER_ID\ndocker compose up -d\n```\n\nYour Phantom is running. Qdrant starts for memory, Ollama pulls the embedding model, and the agent boots. Check health at `http://localhost:3100/health`. With Slack configured, it DMs you when it's ready. Add `RESEND_API_KEY` for email sending. See [Getting Started](docs/getting-started.md) for full setup.\n\n> **Security note, Docker socket mount:** `docker-compose.yaml` mounts\n> `/var/run/docker.sock` into the Phantom container so it can spawn sibling\n> containers (e.g. sandboxed code execution). This is an intentional\n> architectural trade-off: the socket grants the container **root-equivalent\n> access to the Docker daemon**, which means a compromised Phantom process\n> could create, modify, or destroy any container on the host. Mitigations:\n> run Phantom on a dedicated machine or VM (not your personal workstation),\n> and do not expose the host's Docker socket to untrusted workloads. See\n> [docs/security.md](docs/security.md) for the full threat model.\n\n\n### Managed (free)\n\nGet a Phantom on a dedicated VM with nothing to install. Bring your Anthropic API key, we give you the machine.\n\n**[ghostwright.dev/phantom](https://ghostwright.dev/phantom)**\n\n## What People Build with Phantom\n\nPhantom is not just for engineers. It is for anyone who wants an AI that remembers, learns, and builds things you can actually share.\n\n**The key difference:** when an AI runs on your laptop, everything it builds is trapped on localhost. Only you can see it. Phantom runs on a VM with a public domain. Dashboards, tools, pages, APIs - they all get a URL you can send to your team, your manager, or your clients. Your laptop is not a server. Phantom's VM is.\n\n### For People Who Don't Write Code\n\nYou don't need to install developer tools, learn a build system, or figure out hosting. You describe what you want in Slack. Phantom builds it, deploys it on its own machine, and gives you a link.\n\n- **\"Build me a Chrome extension that highlights overdue emails.\"** Phantom builds it and gives you a zip file. You drag it into Chrome. No Xcode, no npm, no terminal. Just install it and go.\n- **\"Make a landing page for my side project.\"** Phantom builds the page, serves it on its public domain, and gives you a URL. Send it to anyone. No hosting setup, no domain configuration.\n- **\"Create a weekly report of our open support tickets.\"** Phantom builds the automation, runs it on a schedule, and emails you the summary every Friday from its own email address.\n- **\"Build a form where the team can submit feature requests.\"** Phantom creates it on its domain, handles submissions, and routes them to Slack.\n\n### Software Engineering\n\n- **Morning standup:** \"Every weekday at 9am, summarize open PRs, CI status, and what needs review.\" Phantom checks GitHub, compiles the summary, and posts it to your team channel.\n- **Codebase onboarding:** \"Clone this repo and give me an architecture overview.\" Phantom reads the code and returns specifics, not generics. \"Next.js 16 with App Router, Drizzle ORM on Neon Postgres, flaky step in the migration check.\"\n- **Infrastructure:** \"Set up a dev Postgres for this project.\" Phantom spins up a Docker container on its own machine, creates the schema, runs migrations, and gives you a connection string. Nothing installed on your laptop.\n- **Data pipelines:** \"Pull from our API every hour and load into Postgres.\" Phantom builds the pipeline, runs the database on its VM, and schedules the cron. You get a connection string.\n- **Custom MCP tools:** \"Create an MCP tool that queries our internal API.\" Phantom builds the tool, registers it, and any Claude Code instance connected to it can call it immediately.\n\n### Sales and Account Management\n\n- **Prospect research:** \"Research these 10 companies and build outreach strategies.\" Phantom gathers intelligence, identifies decision-makers, and creates briefing pages you can share with your team.\n- **Recruiting profiles:** \"Make a profile page for this candidate.\" Phantom researches the person and builds a public profile page you can send to hiring managers. Shareable URL with auth.\n- **Competitor monitoring:** \"Every 2 minutes, check for open-source repos similar to our product.\" Phantom runs a cron job, tracks new entrants, and posts updates to Slack.\n\n### Data and Analytics\n\n- **Build your own analytics stack:** Phantom installs databases, builds ETL pipelines, and registers APIs as MCP tools for future sessions. All on its own machine. (See the ClickHouse story above.)\n- **Shareable dashboards:** \"Track our PR velocity and show it to the team.\" Phantom builds an ECharts dashboard, serves it on a public URL with auth, and sends you the link. Your team bookmarks it. They see the same thing you see.\n- **Data exploration:** \"Load this dataset and let me ask questions about it.\" Phantom creates a queryable environment on its VM. You ask in plain English, it translates to SQL.\n\n### Operations, Marketing, and Everyone Else\n\n- **Automated reports:** \"Email a weekly summary of open issues to team leads every Friday.\" Phantom compiles the report and sends it from its own email address.\n- **Competitor watching:** \"Monitor these five websites for changes and tell me when something updates.\" Phantom checks on a schedule and notifies you in Slack.\n- **Blog drafts:** \"Write a post based on our recent product updates.\" Phantom reads the changelog, writes the draft, and serves it as a page you can review and share with your editor.\n- **Personal coaching:** \"Create a training plan for me.\" Phantom builds a complete plan with a coach persona, served as a page you can reference daily.\n\n### For Everyone\n\n- Remembers what you told it last Monday and uses it on Wednesday.\n- Never asks the same question twice.\n- Gets measurably better at YOUR job every day, not just at being a generic assistant.\n\n## How It's Different\n\nMost AI assistants run on your computer, share your resources, and forget everything between sessions. Phantom was designed around a different assumption: the agent should have its own workspace.\n\n| | Traditional (runs on your machine) | Phantom (its own machine) |\n|--------|-----------------------------------|--------------------------|\n| **Your computer** | Shared with the agent | Yours alone |\n| **Security** | Agent can access your full filesystem | Isolated VM, you control what it sees |\n| **Credentials** | Often stored in plain text config files | AES-256-GCM encrypted, collected via secure forms |\n| **Sharing** | Trapped on localhost, nobody else can see it | Public URL with auth, share with anyone |\n| **Tools** | Fixed set, defined at install time | Creates its own tools at runtime, persists them across restarts |\n| **Availability** | Only when your machine is on | 24/7, runs in the cloud |\n| **Cost** | Uses your CPU and memory | $7-20/month for a dedicated VM |\n\n## Why This Matters\n\n**\"Why does it need its own computer?\"**\n\nBecause you can have an 8GB laptop and give your agent 64GB of RAM for $20/month. Because it can install software, spin up databases, and run services without touching your machine. Because it is always on, even when your laptop is closed. Because everything it builds has a public URL - dashboards, APIs, pages, tools - that you share with a link. Your laptop cannot do that. It does not have a public IP. Phantom's VM does.\n\n**\"Why does self-evolution matter?\"**\n\nBecause Day 1 Phantom is generic. Day 30 Phantom knows your codebase, your deploy process, your PR conventions, and the fact that your biggest client always asks about uptime before renewal. You never repeat yourself. The agent observes, reflects, proposes changes, validates them through a different model (to avoid self-enhancement bias), and evolves. Every version is stored. You can roll back.\n\n**\"Why do dynamic tools matter?\"**\n\nBecause the agent that can only use pre-built tools hits a ceiling. Phantom builds what it needs. One Phantom built a `send_slack_message` tool, registered it, and retired its old workaround. That tool survives restarts. Other agents connecting via MCP can use it too.\n\n## Features\n\n| Feature | Why it matters |\n|---------|----------------|\n| **Its own computer** | Your laptop stays yours. The agent installs software, runs 24/7, and builds infrastructure on its own machine. |\n| **Bring your own model** | Anthropic, Z.AI (GLM-5.1), OpenRouter, Ollama, vLLM, LiteLLM, or any Anthropic Messages API compatible endpoint. Pick your backend in YAML, same agent everywhere. |\n| **Self-evolution** | The agent rewrites its own config after every session, validated by LLM judges. Day 30 knows things Day 1 didn't. |\n| **Persistent memory** | Three tiers of vector memory. Mention something on Monday, it uses it on Wednesday. No re-explaining. |\n| **Dynamic tools** | Creates and registers its own MCP tools at runtime. Tools survive restarts and work across sessions. |\n| **Encrypted secrets** | AES-256-GCM encrypted forms with magic-link auth. No plain-text credentials in config files. |\n| **Email identity** | Every Phantom has its own email address. Send reports to people outside your Slack workspace. |\n| **Web chat** | A full browser-based chat client at `/chat` with SSE streaming, file attachments, and Web Push notifications. No Slack required. |\n| **Shareable pages** | Generates dashboards and tools on a public URL with auth. Share a link, anyone can see it. |\n| **MCP server** | Claude Code connects to your Phantom. Other Phantoms connect to your Phantom. It is an API, not a dead end. |\n\n## Architecture\n\n
\n\n```\n External Clients\n Claude Code | Dashboard | Other Phantoms\n |\n MCP (Streamable HTTP)\n |\n+------------------------------------------+\n| PHANTOM (Bun process) |\n| |\n| Channels Agent Runtime |\n| Slack query() + hooks |\n| Web Chat Prompt Assembler |\n| Telegram base + role + evolved |\n| Email + memory context |\n| Webhook / CLI |\n| |\n| Memory System Self-Evolution Engine |\n| Qdrant 6-step pipeline |\n| Ollama 5-gate validation |\n| 3 collections LLM judges (optional) |\n| |\n| MCP Server Role System |\n| 8 universal YAML-first roles |\n| + role tools Onboarding flow |\n| + dynamic Evolution focus |\n+------------------------------------------+\n | |\n +---------+ +---------+\n | Qdrant | | SQLite |\n | Docker | | Bun |\n +---------+ +---------+\n```\n\n
\n\n## Connect from Claude\n\nFirst, generate a token. The command outputs a bearer token. Save it for the next step.\n\n**Bare metal:**\n```bash\nbun run phantom token create --client claude-code --scope operator\n```\n\n**Docker:**\n```bash\ndocker exec phantom bun run phantom token create --client claude-code --scope operator\n```\n\n**Or just ask your Phantom in Slack:** \"Create an MCP token for Claude Code.\" It will generate the token and give you the config snippet.\n\nThen use the token to connect. Replace `YOUR_TOKEN` below with the token from the command above. For local instances, use `http://localhost:3100/mcp` instead of the `ghostwright.dev` URL.\n\n### Claude Code (CLI)\n\nAdd via the CLI:\n\n```bash\nclaude mcp add phantom https://your-phantom.ghostwright.dev/mcp \\\n --transport http \\\n --header \"Authorization: Bearer YOUR_TOKEN\"\n```\n\nOr add directly to your project's `.mcp.json`:\n\n```json\n{\n \"mcpServers\": {\n \"phantom\": {\n \"type\": \"http\",\n \"url\": \"https://your-phantom.ghostwright.dev/mcp\",\n \"headers\": {\n \"Authorization\": \"Bearer YOUR_TOKEN\"\n }\n }\n }\n}\n```\n\n### Claude Desktop\n\nClaude Desktop only supports stdio transport, so you need [`mcp-remote`](https://www.npmjs.com/package/mcp-remote) to bridge the connection.\n\nAdd this to your `claude_desktop_config.json` (Settings → Developer → Edit Config):\n\n```json\n{\n \"mcpServers\": {\n \"phantom\": {\n \"command\": \"npx\",\n \"args\": [\n \"mcp-remote\",\n \"https://your-phantom.ghostwright.dev/mcp\",\n \"--header\",\n \"Authorization: Bearer YOUR_TOKEN\"\n ]\n }\n }\n}\n```\n\nRestart Claude Desktop after saving. The first connection may take a moment while `mcp-remote` is downloaded.\n\n### Verify\n\nOnce connected, Claude can query your Phantom's memory, ask it questions, check status, and use any dynamic tools the agent has built.\n\n## Self-Evolution\n\nThe core differentiator. After every session:\n\n1. **Observe** - extract corrections, preferences, and domain facts from the conversation\n2. **Critique** - compare session performance against current config\n3. **Generate** - propose minimal, targeted config changes\n4. **Validate** - 5 gates: constitution, regression, size, drift, safety\n5. **Apply** - write approved changes, bump version\n6. **Consolidate** - periodically compress observations into principles\n\nSafety-critical gates use Sonnet as the default cross-model judge (main runs on Opus, so judges run on Sonnet to avoid self-enhancement bias). Operators may opt into Opus judges explicitly for deeper reasoning at higher cost. Triple-judge voting with minority veto: one dissenting judge blocks the change. Every version is stored. You can diff day 1 and day 30. You can roll back.\n\n## The Ghostwright Ecosystem\n\nPhantom is the fourth product in the Ghostwright family:\n\n- **[Ghost OS](https://github.com/ghostwright/ghost-os)** - MCP server for macOS accessibility and screen perception\n- **[Shadow](https://github.com/ghostwright/shadow)** - ambient capture and recall for Mac\n- **[Specter](https://github.com/ghostwright/specter)** - VM provisioning on Hetzner with DNS, TLS, and systemd\n- **Phantom** - the autonomous co-worker\n\n
\nDevelopment Setup\n\n```bash\ngit clone https://github.com/ghostwright/phantom.git\ncd phantom\nbun install\n\n# Start vector DB and embedding model\ndocker compose up -d qdrant ollama\ndocker exec phantom-ollama ollama pull nomic-embed-text\n\n# Initialize config\nbun run phantom init --yes\n\n# Set your API key\nexport ANTHROPIC_API_KEY=sk-ant-...\n\n# Start\nbun run phantom start\n```\n\n```bash\nbun test # 1584 tests\nbun run lint # Biome\nbun run typecheck # tsc --noEmit\n```\n\nSee [docs/getting-started.md](docs/getting-started.md) for detailed Slack setup, .env configuration, VM deployment, and troubleshooting.\n\n

Platforms](#supported-platforms))\n\n## Tech Stack\n\n- **Next.js 16** — App Router, React 19, TypeScript strict\n- **shadcn/ui** — Radix primitives + Tailwind CSS v4\n- **Tailwind CSS v4** — oklch design tokens\n- **Lucide React** — default icons (replaced by extracted SVGs during cloning)\n\n## How It Works\n\nThe `/clone-website` skill runs a multi-phase pipeline:\n\n1. **Reconnaissance** — screenshots, design token extraction, interaction sweep (scroll, click, hover, responsive)\n2. **Foundation** — updates fonts, colors, globals, downloads all assets\n3. **Component Specs** — writes detailed spec files (`docs/research/components/`) with exact computed CSS values, states, behaviors, and content\n4. **Parallel Build** — dispatches builder agents in git worktrees, one per section/component\n5. **Assembly & QA** — merges worktrees, wires up the page, runs visual diff against the original\n\nEach builder agent receives the full component specification inline — exact `getComputedStyle()` values, interaction models, multi-state content, responsive breakpoints, and asset paths. No guessing.\n\n## Use Cases\n\n- **Platform migration** — rebuild a site you own from WordPress/Webflow/Squarespace into a modern Next.js codebase\n- **Lost source code** — your site is live but the repo is gone, the developer left, or the stack is legacy. Get the code back in a modern format\n- **Learning** — deconstruct how production sites achieve specific layouts, animations, and responsive behavior by working with real code\n\n## Not Intended For\n\n- **Phishing or impersonation** — this project must not be used for deceptive purposes, impersonation, or any activity that breaks the law.\n- **Passing off someone's design as your own** — logos, brand assets, and original copy belong to their owners.\n- **Violating terms of service** — some sites explicitly prohibit scraping or reproduction. Check first.\n\n## Project Structure\n\n```\nsrc/\n app/ # Next.js routes\n components/ # React components\n ui/ # shadcn/ui primitives\n icons.tsx # Extracted SVG icons\n lib/utils.ts # cn() utility\n types/ # TypeScript interfaces\n hooks/ # Custom React hooks\npublic/\n images/ # Downloaded images from target\n videos/ # Downloaded videos from target\n seo/ # Favicons, OG images\ndocs/\n research/ # Extraction output & component specs\n design-references/ # Screenshots\nscripts/\n sync-agent-rules.sh # Regenerate agent instruction files\n sync-skills.mjs # Regenerate /clone-website for all platforms\nAGENTS.md # Agent instructions (single source of truth)\nCLAUDE.md # Claude Code config (imports AGENTS.md)\nGEMINI.md # Gemini CLI config (imports AGENTS.md)\n```\n\n## Commands\n\n```bash\nnpm run dev # Start dev server\nnpm run build # Production build\nnpm run lint # ESLint check\nnpm run typecheck # TypeScript check\nnpm run check # Run lint + typecheck + build\n```\n\n### If using docker\n\n```bash\ndocker compose up app --build # build and run the app\ndocker compose up dev --build # run the app in dev mode on port 3001\n```\n\n## Updating for Other Platforms\n\nTwo source-of-truth files power all platform support. Developers and designers looking to rapidly clone, migrate, or learn from existing websites through automated AI-driven reconstruction will find this tool particularly valuable.","description":"Clone any website with one command using AI coding agents","stars":11982,"language":"TypeScript"},{"owner":"marswaveai","repo":"ColaMD","url":"https://github.com/marswaveai/ColaMD","readme":"# ColaMD\n\n**The Agent Native Markdown Editor.**\n\nReal-time collaboration between humans and AI agents — see your agent's changes as they happen.\n\n[![License: MIT](https://img.shields.io/badge/License-MIT-yellow.svg)](https://opensource.org/licenses/MIT)\n[![GitHub release](https://img.shields.io/github/release/marswaveai/colamd.svg)](https://github.com/marswaveai/colamd/releases)\n\n[Download](#download) | [Why ColaMD](#why-colamd) | [Features](#features) | [Development](#development) | [中文](README_CN.md)\n\n---\n\n## Why ColaMD?\n\nAI agents are rewriting how we work. They edit files, generate docs, and produce reports — all in Markdown.\n\nBut how do you **watch** an agent work? You close the file. You reopen it. You wait.\n\n**ColaMD changes this.** Open a `.md` file in ColaMD, let your agent edit it, and watch the content update in real-time — like pair programming with an AI. No refresh, no reload, no friction.\n\nThis is what **Agent Native** means: built from the ground up for a world where humans and agents collaborate on the same files.\n\n## Features\n\n### Agent Native\n\n- **Live Agent Sync** — When an AI agent (Claude Code, Cursor, Copilot, etc.) modifies your `.md` file, ColaMD detects the change and refreshes instantly. This is the core feature.\n- **Agent Activity Indicator** — A subtle dot in the titlebar shows you when an agent is writing: orange breathing pulse while active, green flash when done. You always know if your agent is working.\n- **Cmd+Click Links** — Click any link in the editor to open it in your browser.\n\n### Editor\n\n- **True WYSIWYG** — Type Markdown, see rich text. No split-pane preview.\n- **Smart Line Breaks** — Single newlines render as line breaks, matching how AI agents write Markdown.\n- **Rich Text Copy** — Copy content and paste into WeChat, email, or any rich text editor with formatting preserved.\n- **Minimal by Design** — No toolbar, no sidebar, no distractions. Just your content.\n\n### Themes & Export\n\n- **Themes** — 4 built-in themes + [downloadable themes](themes/) + import custom CSS.\n- **Export** — PDF and HTML.\n- **Cross-platform** — macOS, Windows, Linux.\n\n## Download\n\n> Check [Releases](https://github.com/marswaveai/colamd/releases) for the latest builds.\n\n| Platform | Format |\n|----------|--------|\n| macOS | `.dmg` |\n| Windows | `.exe` |\n| Linux | `.AppImage` / `.deb` |\n\n## How It Works\n\n```\n┌─────────────┐ writes ┌──────────────┐\n│ AI Agent │ ──────────────▶│ .md file │\n│ (Claude, │ │ │\n│ Cursor...) │ └──────┬───────┘\n└─────────────┘ │\n fs.watch detects\n │\n ┌───────▼───────┐\n │ ColaMD │\n │ auto-refresh │\n │ ✨ live! │\n └───────────────┘\n```\n\n1. Open any `.md` file in ColaMD\n2. Let your AI agent edit that file\n3. Watch the content update in real-time — the indicator dot pulses orange while the agent writes\n\nNo configuration needed. It just works.\n\n## What ColaMD Does NOT Do\n\nColaMD is intentionally simple:\n\n- No file manager or workspace\n- No cloud sync or collaboration\n- No AI features built in — it's a **viewer/editor** for AI-generated content\n- No plugin system\n\nOne thing, done well.\n\n## Custom Themes\n\nColaMD supports custom CSS themes. All documents above were created entirely by AI agents using OfficeCLI — no templates, no manual editing.

\n\n## For AI Agents — Get Started in One Line\n\nPaste this into your AI agent's chat — it will read the skill file and install everything automatically:\n\n```\ncurl -fsSL https://officecli.ai/SKILL.md\n```\n\nThat's it. The skill file teaches the agent how to install the binary and use all commands.\n\n> **Technical details:** OfficeCLI ships with a [SKILL.md](SKILL.md) that covers command syntax, architecture, and common pitfalls. After installation, your agent can immediately create, read, and modify any Office document.\n\n## For Humans\n\n**Option A — GUI:** Install [**AionUi**](https://github.com/iOfficeAI/AionUi) — a desktop app that lets you create and edit Office documents through natural language, powered by OfficeCLI under the hood. Just describe what you want, and AionUi handles the rest.\n\n**Option B — CLI:** Download the binary for your platform from [GitHub Releases](https://github.com/iOfficeAI/OfficeCLI/releases), then run:\n\n```bash\nofficecli install\n```\n\nThis copies the binary to your PATH and installs the **officecli skill** into every AI coding agent it detects — Claude Code, Cursor, Windsurf, GitHub Copilot, and more. Your agent can immediately create, read, and edit Office documents on your behalf, no extra configuration needed.\n\n## For Developers — See It Live in 30 Seconds\n\n```bash\n# 1. Install (macOS / Linux)\ncurl -fsSL https://raw.githubusercontent.com/iOfficeAI/OfficeCLI/main/install.sh | bash\n# Windows (PowerShell): irm https://raw.githubusercontent.com/iOfficeAI/OfficeCLI/main/install.ps1 | iex\n\n# 2. Create a blank PowerPoint\nofficecli create deck.pptx\n\n# 3. Start live preview — opens http://localhost:26315 in your browser\nofficecli watch deck.pptx --port 26315\n\n# 4. Open another terminal, add a slide — watch the browser update instantly\nofficecli add deck.pptx / --type slide --prop title=\"Hello, World!\"\n```\n\nThat's it. Every `add`, `set`, or `remove` command you run will refresh the preview in real time. Keep experimenting — the browser is your live feedback loop.\n\n## Quick Start\n\n```bash\n# Create a presentation and add content\nofficecli create deck.pptx\nofficecli add deck.pptx / --type slide --prop title=\"Q4 Report\" --prop background=1A1A2E\nofficecli add deck.pptx '/slide[1]' --type shape \\\n --prop text=\"Revenue grew 25%\" --prop x=2cm --prop y=5cm \\\n --prop font=Arial --prop size=24 --prop color=FFFFFF\n\n# View as outline\nofficecli view deck.pptx outline\n# → Slide 1: Q4 Report\n# → Shape 1 [TextBox]: Revenue grew 25%\n\n# View as HTML — opens a rendered preview in your browser, no server needed\nofficecli view deck.pptx html\n\n# Get structured JSON for any element\nofficecli get deck.pptx '/slide[1]/shape[1]' --json\n```\n\n```json\n{\n \"tag\": \"shape\",\n \"path\": \"/slide[1]/shape[1]\",\n \"attributes\": {\n \"name\": \"TextBox 1\",\n \"text\": \"Revenue grew 25%\",\n \"x\": \"720000\",\n \"y\": \"1800000\"\n }\n}\n```\n\n## Why OfficeCLI?\n\nWhat used to take 50 lines of Python and 3 separate libraries:\n\n```python\nfrom pptx import Presentation\nfrom pptx.util import Inches, Pt\nprs = Presentation()\nslide = prs.slides.add_slide(prs.slide_layouts[0])\ntitle = slide.shapes.title\ntitle.text = \"Q4 Report\"\n# ... 45 more lines ...\nprs.save('deck.pptx')\n```\n\nNow takes one command:\n\n```bash\nofficecli add deck.pptx / --type slide --prop title=\"Q4 Report\"\n```\n\n**What OfficeCLI can do:**\n\n- **Create** documents from scratch -- blank or with content\n- **Read** text, structure, styles, formulas -- in plain text or structured JSON\n- **Analyze** formatting issues, style inconsistencies, and structural problems\n- **Modify** any element -- text, fonts, colors, layout, formulas, charts, images\n- **Reorganize** content -- add, remove, move, copy elements across documents\n\n| Format | Read | Modify | Create |\n|--------|------|--------|--------|\n| Word (.docx) | ✅ | ✅ | ✅ |\n| Excel
