/claude-watch skill for Claude Code\n```\n\n## How It Works\n\n### Event Flow (Mac -> Watch)\n\n1. Claude Code runs a tool (e.g., Edit a file)\n2. The `PostToolUse` HTTP hook fires, POSTing to the bridge server\n3. Bridge pushes the event to all connected SSE clients\n4. The watch/phone receives the SSE event and renders it as a terminal line\n\n### Permission Flow (Mac -> Watch -> Mac)\n\n1. Claude Code hits a permission prompt (e.g., \"Do you want to edit this file?\")\n2. The `PermissionRequest` HTTP hook fires — bridge **blocks** the response\n3. Bridge pushes a `permission-request` SSE event with the question + options\n4. Watch shows the approval sheet with all options as tappable buttons\n5. User taps an option — watch sends the decision back to the bridge via HTTP\n6. Bridge returns the decision to Claude Code's hook — Claude continues or stops\n\n### AskUserQuestion Flow\n\nSame as permission flow, but the hook data includes `tool_input.questions` with dynamic options (label + description). The watch renders these as a scrollable list matching the terminal's numbered choices.\n\n## Claude Code Hooks\n\nThe `setup-hooks.sh` script installs these HTTP hooks globally in `~/.claude/settings.json`:\n\n| Hook Event | Purpose | Blocking? |\n|-----------|---------|-----------|\n| `PostToolUse` | Capture tool output (file reads, edits, commands) | No (async) |\n| `PreToolUse` | Capture tool invocations | No (async) |\n| `PermissionRequest` | Forward permission prompts to watch | **Yes** (up to 10 min) |\n| `Stop` | Detect when Claude finishes responding | No (async) |\n| `PostToolUseFailure` | Capture errors | No (async) |\n| `StopFailure` | Capture API errors | No (async) |\n| `Notification` | Idle/permission notifications | No (async) |\n\n## Configuration\n\n### Bridge Server\n\n| Env Var | Default | Description |\n|---------|---------|-------------|\n| `PORT` | 7860 | Starting port (tries 7860-7869) |\n\n### Removing Hooks\n\n```bash\n./skill/setup-hooks.sh --remove\n```\n\n### Unpairing\n\n- **iPhone:** Settings > Forget Mac\n- **Watch:** Restart the app (credentials clear when bridge restarts)\n\n## Requirements\n\n| Component | Minimum Version |\n|-----------|----------------|\n| macOS | 13.0+ |\n| Node.js | 18+ |\n| Xcode | 16+ |\n| iOS | 17.0 |\n| watchOS | 10.0 |\n| Claude Code | 2.1+ |\n\n## Troubleshooting\n\n### Watch shows \"Bridge not found\"\n- Ensure `node server.js` is running on your Mac\n- Check that your watch is on the same Wi-Fi network\n- Use the \"Enter IP manually\" option with the IP shown in the bridge banner\n\n### Watch shows \"unsupported architecture\"\n- Clean build folder in Xcode (Cmd+Shift+Option+K)\n- Select the correct scheme: **ClaudeWatchWatch** (not ClaudeWatch)\n- Deploy via paired iPhone destination if direct watch deployment fails\n\n### iPhone shows \"Connection failed\"\n- Check that the bridge is running (`curl http://127.0.0.1:7860/status`)\n- The bridge must be on the same LAN as the iPhone\n\n### Permission prompts don't appear on watch\n- Verify hooks are installed: check `~/.claude/settings.json` for hook entries\n- Check bridge logs for \"Hook: PermissionRequest received\"\n- Ensure the watch is connected to the bridge (green status dot)\n\n### Bridge exits immediately\n- The bridge no longer auto-spawns Claude. It waits for events from hooks.\n- Start Claude Code in a separate terminal — hooks will forward events automatically.\n\n## License\n\nMIT\n","summary":" Agent Watch enables developers to monitor and control Claude Code sessions directly from their Apple Watch, displaying live terminal output and allowing users to approve file edits, run commands, or respond to prompts from their wrist via an intuitive SwiftUI interface. \n\n🔥 We have built a vllm website to help you get started with vllm. Please visit [vllm.ai](https://vllm.ai) to learn more.\nFor events, please visit [vllm.ai/events](https://vllm.ai/events) to join us.\n\n---\n\n## About\n\nvLLM is a fast and easy-to-use library for LLM inference and serving.\n\nOriginally developed in the [Sky Computing Lab](https://sky.cs.berkeley.edu) at UC Berkeley, vLLM has evolved into a community-driven project with contributions from both academia and industry.\n\nvLLM is fast with:\n\n- State-of-the-art serving throughput\n- Efficient management of attention key and value memory with [**PagedAttention**](https://blog.vllm.ai/2023/06/20/vllm.html)\n- Continuous batching of incoming requests\n- Fast model execution with CUDA/HIP graph\n- Quantizations: [GPTQ](https://arxiv.org/abs/2210.17323), [AWQ](https://arxiv.org/abs/2306.00978), [AutoRound](https://arxiv.org/abs/2309.05516), INT4, INT8, and FP8\n- Optimized CUDA kernels, including integration with FlashAttention and FlashInfer\n- Speculative decoding\n- Chunked prefill\n\nvLLM is flexible and easy to use with:\n\n- Seamless integration with popular Hugging Face models\n- High-throughput serving with various decoding algorithms, including *parallel sampling*, *beam search*, and more\n- Tensor, pipeline, data and expert parallelism support for distributed inference\n- Streaming outputs\n- OpenAI-compatible API server\n- Support for NVIDIA GPUs, AMD CPUs and GPUs, Intel CPUs and GPUs, PowerPC CPUs, Arm CPUs, and TPU. Additionally, support for diverse hardware plugins such as Intel Gaudi, IBM Spyre and Huawei Ascend.\n- Prefix caching support\n- Multi-LoRA support\n\nvLLM seamlessly supports most popular open-source models on HuggingFace, including:\n\n- Transformer-like LLMs (e.g., Llama)\n- Mixture-of-Expert LLMs (e.g., Mixtral, Deepseek-V2 and V3)\n- Embedding Models (e.g., E5-Mistral)\n- Multi-modal LLMs (e.g., LLaVA)\n\nFind the full list of supported models [here](https://docs.vllm.ai/en/latest/models/supported_models.html).\n\n## TurboQuant Fork Highlights\n\nThis fork extends vLLM's experimental TurboQuant KV-cache path with a workflow\naimed at supported CUDA workstation GPUs:\n\n- TurboQuant KV cache on `RTX A6000 / SM86` and `GB10 / SM121`\n- `turboquant25` and `turboquant35` KV-cache recipes on the Triton attention backend\n- Per-layer TurboQuant metadata loading from `--turboquant-metadata-path` or a local model-side `turboquant_kv.json`\n- Tensor-parallel metadata slicing for replicated and partitioned KV-head layouts\n- Kernel tuning for supported CUDA targets and a Triton prefill fast path for common head sizes\n- Benchmark and bring-up docs for long-context TurboQuant comparisons and 4x A6000 serving\n\nStart here for the fork-specific docs:\n\n- [Quantized KV Cache docs](docs/features/quantization/quantized_kvcache.md)\n- [TurboQuant on RTX A6000 and CUDA 12.8](docs/features/quantization/turboquant_a6000.md)\n- [TurboQuant comparison benchmark](benchmarks/run_turboquant_gb10_compare.sh)\n\n## Getting Started\n\nInstall vLLM with `pip` or [from source](https://docs.vllm.ai/en/latest/getting_started/installation/gpu/index.html#build-wheel-from-source):\n\n```bash\npip install vllm\n```\n\nFor TurboQuant on this fork, use a source build instead of precompiled wheels:\n\n```bash\nuv venv --python 3.12\nsource .venv/bin/activate\n\nexport CUDA_HOME=/usr/local/cuda-12.8\nexport PATH=\"${CUDA_HOME}/bin:${PATH}\"\nexport VLLM_TARGET_DEVICE=cuda\nexport VLLM_USE_PRECOMPILED=0\nexport VLLM_MAIN_CUDA_VERSION=12.8\n\nuv pip install -e .\n```\n\nExample TurboQuant serve command:\n\n```bash\n.venv/bin/vllm serve /models/target \\\n --tensor-parallel-size 4 \\\n --attention-backend TRITON_ATTN \\\n --kv-cache-dtype turboquant35 \\\n --enable-turboquant \\\n --turboquant-metadata-path /models/target/turboquant_kv.json\n```\n\nVisit our [documentation](https://docs.vllm.ai/en/latest/) to learn more.\n\n- \n\n---\n\n## 🦞 Part of the MyClaw.ai Ecosystem\n\n\n\n\n\n\n
\n \n\n\n**[MyClaw.ai](https://myclaw.ai)** is the AI personal assistant platform everyone's obsessed with — a fully-featured OpenClaw Agent running 24/7 on your own dedicated server. Not a chatbot. Not a wrapper. A real agent with full code control, internet access, cron jobs, file systems, databases, and tool integrations. Think of it as hiring a brilliant assistant who never sleeps, never forgets*, and can actually *do things*.\n\n*With Auto-Dream installed, they literally never forget.\n\n
\n\n### Why MyClaw Changes Everything\n\nMost AI tools give you a chat window. MyClaw gives you a **server**.\n\nEvery MyClaw instance runs [OpenClaw](https://github.com/openclaw/openclaw) — the open-source AI agent runtime — on dedicated infrastructure. Your agent has:\n\n- 🖥️ **A full Linux server** — not a sandbox, not a container, a real machine\n- 🌐 **Unrestricted internet** — browse, scrape, call APIs, send messages\n- ⏰ **Cron & background tasks** — your agent works while you sleep\n- 📁 **Persistent file system** — workspace, memory, configs, all yours\n- 🧩 **Skill ecosystem** — install new abilities from [ClawHub](https://myclaw.ai/skills) in one command\n- 🔌 **Channel integrations** — Telegram, Discord, Slack, WhatsApp, and more\n- 🔒 **Your data, your server** — no shared infrastructure, no data mining\n\nThis is why Auto-Dream exists. Because when your AI agent has a persistent server, persistent files, and persistent relationships with you — **memory isn't a nice-to-have. It's the foundation of intelligence.**\n\n---\n\n## The Problem\n\nEvery AI agent forgets. Session ends, context gone. Files pile up. What was that decision from two weeks ago? Which workflow worked last time? Your agent has amnesia — functional, but forgetting everything the moment it sleeps.\n\n**Auto-Dream fixes this.** Like the human brain consolidating memories during sleep, Auto-Dream runs periodic \"dream cycles\" that scan, extract, organize, score, link, and prune your agent's knowledge — automatically, safely, and intelligently.\n\n### Why This Matters for MyClaw Users\n\nYour MyClaw agent runs 24/7. It handles your projects, tracks your decisions, remembers your preferences, manages your workflows. Over weeks and months, it accumulates thousands of daily log entries. Without Auto-Dream, that knowledge sits in raw files — unsorted, unscored, disconnected. Your agent has the data but can't *think* about it.\n\nAuto-Dream transforms your agent from a tool that executes commands into a partner that **understands context, learns from history, and connects the dots you didn't see**.\n\n## Why This Is Different\n\n| Feature | Claude Code CLAUDE.md | Typical Memory Plugins | **Auto-Dream** |\n|---------|----------------------|----------------------|----------------|\n| Memory layers | 1 flat file | 1 file or key-value | **5 cognitive layers** |\n| Scoring | ❌ | ❌ | **Importance × Recency × References** |\n| Forgetting | Manual cleanup | Delete or nothing | **Gradual decay + archival** |\n| Knowledge graph | ❌ | ❌ | **Linked entries + reachability** |\n| Health monitoring | ❌ | ❌ | **5-metric score + trend tracking** |\n| Cross-instance | ❌ | ❌ | **Export/import/merge bundles** |\n| Dashboard | ❌ | ❌ | **Interactive HTML with charts** |\n\n## Architecture\n\n```\n┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ │\n│ ┌─────────────┐ ┌──────────────┐ ┌───────────────────┐ │\n│ │ COLLECT │──▶│ CONSOLIDATE │──▶│ EVALUATE │ │\n│ │ │ │ │ │ │ │\n│ │ Scan 7 days │ │ Route layers │ │ Score importance │ │\n│ │ Flag markers│ │ Semantic dedup│ │ Forgetting curve │ │\n│ │ Extract │ │ Assign IDs │ │ Health metrics │ │\n│ │ insights │ │ Link relations│ │ Generate insights │ │\n│ └─────────────┘ └──────────────┘ └───────────────────┘ │\n│ │\n│ ☽ Dream Cycle ☾ │\n└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n │\n ┌───────────────┼───────────────┐\n ▼ ▼ ▼\n ┌──────────────┐ ┌─────────────┐ ┌──────────────┐\n │ 📊 Dashboard │ │ 🔔 Notify │ │ 📝 Dream Log │\n │ HTML + Charts│ │ Push to chat│ │ Append report│\n └──────────────┘ └─────────────┘ └──────────────┘\n```\n\n### Five Memory Layers\n\n| Layer | Storage | What Goes Here |\n|-------|---------|---------------|\n| **Working** | LCM plugin (optional, detected at setup) | Real-time context compression & semantic recall |\n| **Episodic** | `memory/episodes/*.md` | Project narratives, event timelines, story arcs |\n| **Long-term** | `MEMORY.md` | Facts, decisions, people, milestones, strategy |\n| **Procedural** | `memory/procedures.md` | Workflows, preferences, tool patterns, shortcuts |\n| **Index** | `memory/index.json` | Metadata, importance scores, relations, health stats |\n\n## Features\n\n### 🧠 Cognitive Dream Cycle\n\nRuns automatically via cron (default: 4 AM daily). Three phases:\n\n1. **Collect** — Scans unconsolidated daily logs (last 7 days), detects priority markers (`⚠️ PERMANENT`, `🔥 HIGH`, `📌 PIN`, ``), extracts decisions / people / facts / projects / lessons / procedures / open threads\n\n2. **Consolidate** — Routes each insight to the correct memory layer, performs semantic deduplication, assigns unique IDs (`mem_NNN`), creates relation links between connected entries\n\n3. **Evaluate** — Scores importance using `base_weight × recency × reference_boost / 8.0`, applies forgetting curves (>90 days + low importance → archived, never deleted), calculates 5-metric health score, generates 1–3 non-obvious insights, writes dream report, sends notification\n\n### 📊 Importance Scoring\n\nEvery entry gets a score on every dream cycle:\n\n```\nimportance = (base_weight × recency_factor × reference_boost) / 8.0\n```\n\n- **Recency**: `max(0.1, 1.0 - days/180)` — gradual decay over 6 months\n- **References**: `log₂(count + 1)` — logarithmic boost for frequently-referenced entries\n- **Markers**: `🔥 HIGH` doubles base weight; `⚠️ PERMANENT` always scores 1.0\n\n### 📉 Intelligent Forgetting\n\nMemories aren't deleted — they're gracefully archived:\n- Entry must be >90 days unreferenced AND importance < 0.3\n- Compressed to a one-line summary in `memory/archive.md`\n- Original ID preserved for relation tracking\n- `⚠️ PERMANENT` and `📌 PIN` entries are immune\n\n### 🕸️ Knowledge Graph\n\nEntries are linked by semantic relations. The reachability metric measures graph connectivity:\n- Union-find algorithm across all entry relations\n- Detects isolated knowledge clusters\n- Suggests cross-references to improve coherence\n\n### 🩺 Health Score (5 Metrics)\n\n```\nhealth = (freshness×0.25 + coverage×0.25 + coherence×0.2 + efficiency×0.15 + reachability×0.15) × 100\n```\n\n| Metric | What It Measures |\n|--------|-----------------|\n| **Freshness** | % of entries referenced in last 30 days |\n| **Coverage** | % of knowledge categories updated in last 14 days |\n| **Coherence** | % of entries with at least one relation link |\n| **Efficiency** | How concise MEMORY.md stays (inversely proportional to line count) |\n| **Reachability** | How well-connected the memory graph is |\n\n### 🔔 Push Notifications\n\nDream results delivered to your chat automatically:\n\n| Level | What You Get |\n|-------|-------------|\n| `silent` | Nothing — logged to dream-log.md only |\n| `summary` | `🌀 Health: 82/100 \\| +5 new, ~3 updated, -1 archived \\| 💡 Top insight` |\n| `full` | Complete dream report with all sections |\n\n### 📊 Interactive Dashboard\n\nA zero-dependency HTML dashboard with:\n- Animated health gauge (0–100)\n- 5 metric cards with color-coded status\n- Memory distribution donut chart\n- Importance histogram\n- Health trend line chart (last 30 cycles)\n- Force-directed knowledge graph visualization\n- Recent changes, insights, suggestions, stale entries\n\nGenerate it: *\"Show memory dashboard\"*\n\n### 🔄 Cross-Instance Migration\n\nMove memories between MyClaw instances:\n\n```\n\"Export memory bundle\" → memory/export-2026-03-28.json\n\"Import memory bundle\" → merges with existing (newer wins)\n\"Export only procedures\" → selective layer export\n```\n\nPortable JSON bundle format with full metadata, conflict resolution, and pre-import backup. Perfect for users managing multiple MyClaw instances or upgrading to a new server.\n\n### 🔮 Dream Insights\n\nAfter each cycle, 1–3 non-obvious observations:\n- **Pattern connections** — *\"Project X's strategy mirrors what worked for Project Y\"*\n- **Temporal trends** — *\"Strategic decisions cluster on Mondays — weekly planning detected\"*\n- **Gap detection** — *\"No lessons recorded for last 4 projects — retrospectives overdue\"*\n- **Trend alerts** — *\"Health declining 3 cycles: 85→79→72 — stale entries accumulating\"*\n- **Density analysis** — *\"mem_042 referenced by 8 entries but has no outbound links\"*\n\n## Quick Start\n\n### Install\n\n**Via ClawHub (recommended):**\n```bash\nclawhub install openclaw-auto-dream\n```\n\n**Via your MyClaw agent (easiest):**\n> Just tell your agent: *\"Install Auto-Dream\"* — it handles everything.\n\n**Manual:**\n```bash\ngit clone https://github.com/LeoYeAI/openclaw-auto-dream.git \\\n ~/.openclaw/workspace/skills/openclaw-auto-dream\n```\n\n### Setup\n\nTell your agent: **\"Set up Auto-Dream\"**\n\nThe agent will:\n1. Create a cron job (default: daily at 4 AM in your timezone)\n2. Initialize `memory/index.json` with v3.0 schema\n3. Ask your preferred notification level\n4. Run the first dream cycle\n\n### Manual Trigger\n\n- *\"Run memory maintenance\"*\n- *\"Consolidate my memories\"*\n- *\"Dream now\"*\n\n### Dashboard\n\n- *\"Show memory dashboard\"*\n- *\"Generate memory dashboard\"*\n\n## Dream Report Example\n\n```markdown\n## 🌀 Dream Report — 2026-03-28 04:00 UTC\n\n### 📊 Stats\n- Scanned: 7 files | New: 5 | Updated: 3 | Pruned: 1\n- MEMORY.md: 142 lines | Episodes: 2 | Procedures: 8 entries\n\n### 🧠 Health: 76/100\n- Freshness: 72% | Coverage: 80% | Coherence: 55% | Efficiency: 90% | Reachability: 40%\n\n### 🔮 Insights\n- [Pattern] MyClaw growth trajectory mirrors early Shopify — consider their Series A playbook\n- [Gap] No episode file for infrastructure migration — 12 related entries scattered across daily logs\n\n### 📝 Changes\n- [New] mem_089 — Product roadmap decision: prioritize mobile SDK\n- [Updated] mem_042 — Team headcount updated: 30 → 35\n- [Archived] mem_015 — Old staging API endpoint (superseded 95 days ago)\n\n### 💡 Suggestions\n- Coherence at 55% — link mem_089 to related project entries\n- Reachability at 0.40 — 3 isolated memory clusters detected; add cross-references\n```\n\n## Safety\n\n| Rule | Why |\n|------|-----|\n| Never delete daily logs | Immutable source of truth |\n| Never remove `⚠️ PERMANENT` | User protection is absolute |\n| Episodes are append-only | Narrative history preserved forever |\n| Auto-backup on >30% change | Prevents accidental corruption |\n| Index backup every cycle | Always recoverable |\n| Secrets policy | Only consolidates secrets already present |\n\n## Working (LCM) → Episodic → Long-term → Procedural → Index\n- **Three-phase dream cycle**: Collect → Consolidate → Evaluate\n- **Importance scoring**: base_weight × recency × reference_boost with forgetting curve\n- **Memory index**: `index.json` with IDs, timestamps, relations, reference counts\n- **User markers**: ⚠️ PERMANENT, 🔥 HIGH, 📌 PIN, ``\n\n### v1.0.0 — Initial Release It implements periodic \"dream cycles\" that automatically consolidate, score, and organize agent experiences across five memory layers while employing forgetting curves and knowledge graphs to maintain relevant information. Unlike simple file storage, this system provides importance scoring, health dashboards, and intelligent pruning to ensure agents retain critical context and relationships over time. It is particularly valuable for MyClaw.ai users and others running persistent OpenClaw agents who require durable memory across long-running tasks and conversations.","description":"Automatic memory consolidation for OpenClaw agents — like sleep for your AI. \n \n

\n\n# ZINC — Zig INferenCe Engine\n\n

\n \n \n \n \n \n \n \n \n \n \n \n \n \n \n \n \n

\n\n> Local LLM inference on AMD GPUs and Apple Silicon — no ROCm, no MLX, one binary.\n\n

\n \n
\n 35B parameter model running locally — Zig + Vulkan/Metal, no ROCm, no MLX\n

\n\n## Supported Platforms\n\n| Platform | GPU | Backend | Status |\n|----------|-----|---------|--------|\n| **Linux** | AMD RDNA4 (RX 9070, AI PRO R9700) | Vulkan | Primary — hand-tuned shaders |\n| **Linux** | AMD RDNA3 (RX 7900 XTX, etc.) | Vulkan | Supported |\n| **macOS** | Apple Silicon (M1, M2, M3, M4, M5) | Metal | Supported — native MSL shaders |\n\n## Start Here\n\nWorks the same on Linux (AMD GPU) and macOS (Apple Silicon):\n\n```bash\ngit clone https://github.com/zolotukhin/zinc.git\ncd zinc\nzig build -Doptimize=ReleaseFast\n\n# On RDNA4 Linux, enable cooperative matrix\nexport RADV_PERFTEST=coop_matrix # skip on macOS\n\n# Verify GPU, shaders, and runtime\n./zig-out/bin/zinc --check\n\n# See which models fit this machine\n./zig-out/bin/zinc model list\n\n# Download a model\n./zig-out/bin/zinc model pull qwen3-8b-q4k-m\n\n# Run a prompt (--chat applies the model's chat template for instruct models)\n./zig-out/bin/zinc --model-id qwen3-8b-q4k-m --prompt \"Hello\" --chat\n\n# Or open the chat UI in your browser\n./zig-out/bin/zinc chat\n```\n\nThe server exposes the built-in chat UI at `/` and an OpenAI-compatible API at `/v1`.\n\n## What Works Today\n\n- Single-stream CLI inference on the validated models listed below\n- OpenAI-compatible `/v1` API with streaming\n- Built-in browser chat UI with thinking mode support\n- Managed model workflow: `list`, `pull`, `use`, `active`, `rm`\n- `zinc chat` — start server and open browser in one command\n- **AMD path**: RDNA4-tuned Vulkan shaders (wave64, cooperative matrix, fused ops)\n- **Apple Silicon path**: native Metal shaders (MSL, zero-copy mmap, simdgroup ops)\n- Auto-detection: ZINC picks the right backend (Vulkan or Metal) at build time\n\n## Still Rough\n\n- Continuous batching and multi-tenant serving are still roadmap work\n- The supported-model list is intentionally narrow\n- Apple Silicon performance tuning is ongoing (RDNA4 path is more mature)\n\n## The Problem\n\nConsumer GPUs have the hardware for fast LLM inference — bandwidth, compute, VRAM — but the software doesn't use it:\n\n- **AMD RDNA3/RDNA4**: ROCm doesn't support them. vLLM requires ROCm. llama.cpp's Vulkan path has no RDNA-specific tuning. These $500–1500 cards sit idle.\n- **Apple Silicon**: MLX and llama.cpp Metal work, but leave performance on the table. No engine is built from scratch around Metal's strengths (unified memory, simdgroup ops, zero-copy mmap).\n\n## The Solution\n\nZINC builds an inference engine tuned for the hardware you actually have.\n\n**Hand-tuned shaders for each platform.** On AMD: wave64, cooperative matrix, architecture-aware tiling via Vulkan compute. On Apple Silicon: native MSL kernels with simdgroup reductions, zero-copy model loading, and Metal pipeline tuning. Not a generic backend that happens to run — built to extract real performance from each GPU.\n\n**One binary, no driver stack.** No ROCm, no CUDA, no Python. Build with Zig, point at a GGUF, run inference. The right backend (Vulkan or Metal) is selected automatically at build time.\n\n**Drop-in compatible.** OpenAI-compatible API, built-in chat UI, managed model catalog. Point your existing client at it and it works.\n\n## Supported Models\n\nThe list below matches the current managed model catalog, not a broader wishlist.\n\n- [Qwen3.5 35B-A3B UD Q4_K_XL](https://huggingface.co/unsloth/Qwen3.5-35B-A3B-GGUF) — supported on AMD RDNA4 32 GB and Apple Silicon\n- [Qwen3.6 35B-A3B UD Q4_K_XL](https://huggingface.co/unsloth/Qwen3.6-35B-A3B-GGUF) — experimental on AMD RDNA4 32 GB and Apple Silicon\n- [OpenAI GPT-OSS 20B Q4_K_M](https://huggingface.co/bartowski/openai_gpt-oss-20b-GGUF) — supported on Apple Silicon\n- [Qwen3 8B Q4_K_M](https://huggingface.co/unsloth/Qwen3-8B-GGUF) — supported on AMD RDNA4 32 GB and Apple Silicon\n- [Gemma 4 31B Q4_K_M](https://huggingface.co/unsloth/gemma-4-31B-it-GGUF) — supported on AMD RDNA4 32 GB and Apple Silicon\n- [Gemma 4 12B (26B-A4B MoE) Q4_K_M](https://huggingface.co/unsloth/gemma-4-26B-A4B-it-GGUF) — experimental on AMD RDNA4 32 GB and Apple Silicon\n\n- Use `zinc model list --json` for machine-readable model metadata\n- Current throughput and latency numbers live on the public benchmarks page: [zolotukhin.ai/zinc/benchmarks](https://zolotukhin.ai/zinc/benchmarks)\n\n**Quantization formats**: Q4_K, Q5_K, Q6_K, Q8_0, Q5_0, MXFP4, F16, F32\n\n## Quick Start\n\n### Prerequisites\n\n| Tool | Install |\n|------|---------|\n| Zig 0.15.2+ | [ziglang.org/download](https://ziglang.org/download/) |\n| Vulkan loader + tools | `apt install libvulkan-dev vulkan-tools` (Linux) or `brew install vulkan-loader vulkan-headers` (macOS) |\n| `glslc` on Linux | `apt install glslc` |\n| Bun for tests and the docs site | `curl -fsSL https://bun.sh/install \\| bash` |\n\n**Important**: On Linux with RDNA4, newer `glslc` releases can cause a large regression. Use the system package version.\n\n### Build ZINC\n\n```bash\ngit clone https://github.com/zolotukhin/zinc.git\ncd zinc\n\n# Build the CLI and server\n# macOS: shaders are skipped\n# Linux: shaders are compiled automatically\nzig build -Doptimize=ReleaseFast\n```\n\nThe binary is placed in `zig-out/bin/zinc`. Compiled SPIR-V shaders go to `zig-out/share/zinc/shaders/`.\nUse `ReleaseFast` for any performance measurement or server deployment. Plain `zig build` is not a fair throughput baseline.\n\n### Run a Preflight Check First\n\nBefore your first prompt, run `--check`. The target state is a clean `READY [OK]` run with no warnings.\n\n```bash\n# General machine + Vulkan + shader preflight\n./zig-out/bin/zinc --check\n\n# Recommended on RDNA4 before measuring performance\nexport RADV_PERFTEST=coop_matrix\n./zig-out/bin/zinc --check\n\n# Check one exact GGUF file\n./zig-out/bin/zinc --check -m /path/to/model.gguf\n\n# Check one managed catalog model by id\n./zig-out/bin/zinc --check --model-id qwen35-35b-a3b-q4k-xl\n```\n\n`--check` verifies:\n\n- host environment and RDNA4-specific shell hints\n- compiled shader assets\n- Vulkan device discovery and the selected GPU\n- GGUF metadata when you pass `-m /path/to/model.gguf`\n- managed-model compatibility when you pass `--model-id `\n- estimated single-GPU VRAM fit for the current runtime\n\nIf `--check` reports warnings, treat them as setup work to finish before judging runtime behavior. For the full walkthrough, see [Running ZINC](docs/RUNNING_ZINC.md) and [Hardware requirements](docs/HARDWARE_REQUIREMENTS.md).\n\n### Choosing Models\n\nThe README keeps the supported-model section concise and leaves the full managed-model workflow to the docs.\n\nUse these for model selection, cache management, and API details:\n\n- [Running ZINC](https://zolotukhin.ai/zinc/docs/running-zinc)\n- [Serving HTTP API](https://zolotukhin.ai/zinc/docs/api)\n\n### Run a Prompt\n\n```bash\n./zig-out/bin/zinc -m /path/to/model.gguf --prompt \"The capital of France is\"\n```\n\n### Run the Server\n\nStart the server — no `--prompt` flag means server mode:\n\n```bash\n./zig-out/bin/zinc -m /path/to/model.gguf -p 8080\n```\n\nThen open **http://localhost:8080/** in your browser for the built-in chat interface.\n\n### Use the API\n\nZINC exposes an OpenAI-compatible API at `/v1`.\n\nFor the actual request examples and SDK usage, use the website docs instead of the README:\n\n- [Running ZINC](https://zolotukhin.ai/zinc/docs/running-zinc) for CLI, server mode, and first-run examples\n- [Serving HTTP API](https://zolotukhin.ai/zinc/docs/api) for `curl`, OpenAI SDK examples, endpoint behavior, and response shapes\n\nThe built-in chat UI is served at `/`, the API is under `/v1`, and the health endpoint is `/health`.\n\n## Development\n\nFor building, testing, debugging, benchmarking, graph export, and contributing — see the **[Development Guide](./docs/DEVELOPMENT.md)** ([web version](https://zolotukhin.ai/zinc/docs/development)).\n\nQuick start:\n\n```bash\nzig build -Doptimize=ReleaseFast # build\nzig build test # run all tests\n./zig-out/bin/zinc --check # verify GPU/runtime setup\n```\n\nSee also: [CONTRIBUTING.md](./CONTRIBUTING.md) · [Code of Conduct](./CODE_OF_CONDUCT.md)\n\n## Architecture\n\n

\n\n## Benchmarks\n\nCurrent throughput and latency numbers live on the public benchmarks page:\n\n- [ZINC Benchmarks](https://zolotukhin.ai/zinc/benchmarks)\n\nFor the local benchmark commands, harnesses, and methodology, use the development docs:\n\n- [Development Guide](./docs/DEVELOPMENT.md)\n- [Running ZINC](./docs/RUNNING_ZINC.md)\n\n## Current Status\n\n| Component | Status |\n|-----------|--------|\n| Vulkan infrastructure | Done |\n| GGUF parser + model loader | Done |\n| GPU detection (RDNA3/4) | Done |\n| Native BPE tokenizer (from GGUF) | Done |\n| GLSL compute shaders (16) | Done |\n| Compute graph + architecture builders | Done |\n| Forward pass (decode loop) | Working — 37.95 tok/s on RDNA4 and 35.61 tok/s on Apple M4 Max for Qwen3.5-35B-A3B-UD |\n| GPU SSM shaders + cmd batching | Done — Metal and Vulkan decode paths are both above 35 tok/s on the validated 35B boxes |\n| HTTP server + OpenAI API | Done — 35B raw API ~33.5 tok/s on RDNA4 and ~34.7 tok/s on Apple M4 Max; reasoning chat still slower |\n| Continuous batching | Phase 4 |\n| TurboQuant KV compression | Phase 5 |\n\nValidated on AMD Radeon AI PRO R9700 (RDNA4): Vulkan 1.3 init, GGUF parsing, 21 GB model loaded to VRAM, 723-node MoE graph built, coherent inference output verified against CPU reference.\n\n## Next Steps\n\nThe next push is from \"raw decode above 30\" to \"reasoning workloads above 30 and better aggregate GPU utilization\":\n\n1. **Close the chat/reasoning gap** — benchmark longer chat prompts, template overhead, stop behavior, and TTFT so `/v1/chat/completions` tracks closer to the raw decode path.\n2. **Make profiling representative** — `--profile` is still too intrusive in `ReleaseFast`, so it is not yet the right leaderboard tool for apples-to-apples throughput claims.\n3. **Reduce hot-path descriptor churn** — reuse bindings and trim per-token Vulkan setup in the decode loop.\n4. **Tune the actual hot shapes** — focus on medium/small decode kernels, not just the vocab projection.\n5. **Increase aggregate throughput with batching** — if the goal is to drive bandwidth utilization much higher, concurrency is the right lever.\n\n## License\n\nMIT\n","summary":" ZINC is a lightweight, single-binary LLM inference engine written in Zig that enables high-performance local AI on AMD RDNA3/RDNA4 GPUs and Apple Silicon Macs without requiring ROCm or MLX dependencies. It achieves hardware-specific optimization through hand-tuned Vulkan compute shaders featuring cooperative matrix operations for AMD cards, and native Metal Performance Shaders with zero-copy memory mapping for Apple Silicon. The tool includes an OpenAI-compatible API endpoint, a built-in browser-based chat interface, and simple CLI commands for model management. It serves users who want efficient local LLM inference on consumer hardware that existing frameworks often fail to optimize for or support adequately.","description":"Zig INferenCe Engine — Local LLM inference on AMD GPUs and Apple Silicon","stars":317,"language":"Zig"}]
